{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"‘The Art of The Mitchells vs. The Machines’ is Packed with Dazzling Illustrations, Animation Insights & More","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=671943","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-671950 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artwork-katievision-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"The Art of The Mitchells vs The Machines\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artwork-katievision.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artwork-katievision-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>How do you follow up an innovative, visually stunning movie like <em>Spider-Man: Into the Spider-Verse</em>? For Sony Pictures Animation and producers <strong>Phil Lord &#38; Chris Miller</strong>, the answer was something completely original that pushed the boundaries of animation and delivered a heartfelt, exciting story about a dysfunctional family coming together during a robot apocalypse.</p>\n<p>The result was <strong><em>The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em></strong>, a movie from <em>Gravity Falls</em> duo <strong>Michael Rianda</strong> and <strong>Jeff Rowe</strong> that was both out of this world and profoundly personal in a number of ways. In the new book, <strong><em>The Art of The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em></strong>, not only do you learn how this incredible adventure came to be after years of development and animation, but you&#8217;ll see astounding spreads of artwork that reveal how much imagination and creative freedom was put into this movie, including elements that didn&#8217;t make it into the final cut.<span id=\"more-671943\"></span></p>\n\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/the-art-of-the-mitchells-vs-the-machines-book-review/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-familysketch/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"465\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-familysketch-360x465.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"The Art of The Mitchells vs The Machines\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-familysketch-360x465.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-familysketch.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/the-art-of-the-mitchells-vs-the-machines-book-review/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-digitalphoto/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"465\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-digitalphoto-360x465.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"The Art of The Mitchells vs The Machines\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-digitalphoto-360x465.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-digitalphoto.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n\n<p>With a movie from the producers of <em>Cloudy with a Chance of Meatballs</em>, <em>The LEGO Movie</em>, and <em>Spider-Man: Into the Spider-Verse</em>, you know you&#8217;re in for a spectacular adventure full of mesmerizing visuals, witty comedy, and a big beating heart. But in the case of <em>The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em>, the movie actually starts with director/co-writer <strong>Michael Rianda</strong> and his <em>Gravity Falls</em> cohort <strong>Jeff Rowe</strong>, who co-directed and co-wrote the film with him.</p>\n<p><em>The Art of The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em> begins by recalling how Rianda and Rowe looked back at their experiences growing up as creative individuals struggling to find a place to belong, something that would appeal to many of the artists working on this movie. Rianda in particular pulled many personal details from his father&#8217;s contentious relationship with technology and love of the outdoors. And both of the filmmakers hoped to tell a story about a family that was far from perfect, one that lived in a messy, middle-class, Michigan home. It just so happens that this family gets caught up in the robot apocalypse and somehow become the only people who can stop it.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-671949 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artwork-livingroom-700x453.jpg\" alt=\"The Art of The Mitchells vs The Machines\" width=\"700\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artwork-livingroom-700x453.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artwork-livingroom-360x233.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artwork-livingroom-768x497.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artwork-livingroom.jpg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Insights from the development of this sci-fi adventure come from key crew members such as production designer <strong>Lindsey Olivares</strong>, head of story <strong>Guillermo Martinez</strong>, art director <strong>Toby Wilson</strong>, lead color designer <strong>David R. Bleich</strong>, VFX supervisor <strong>Mike Lasker</strong>, and head of character animation <strong>Alan Hawkins</strong>. That&#8217;s all accompanied by a rich tapestry of storyboards, concept art, rough sketches, and more, each piece providing a new look at this eccentric family.</p>\n<p>The artwork that accompanies the behind-the-scenes anecdotes literally illustrates that no idea was too off-the-wall for consideration in <em>The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em>. The character designs for the Mitchell family alone show how much exploration was done to give this film just the right kind of quirk and originality to stand out from the rest of the animated family adventures out there. There&#8217;s a two-page spread in this book that reveals the wide variety of hairstyles, wardrobes, and facial features that were considered for the main character Katie alone (trust me, they&#8217;re more varied than what you see below).</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-671951 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-katie-design-700x425.jpg\" alt=\"The Art of The Mitchells vs The Machines\" width=\"700\" height=\"425\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-katie-design-700x425.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-katie-design-360x219.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-katie-design-768x466.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvsthemachines-artbook-katie-design.jpg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><em>The Art of The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em> highlights the progression from naturalistic and irregular imagery representative of The Mitchells to the polished, polygonal design of PAL&#8217;s robots and their techno-world that starts to take over Earth. It explores the traits of the narrative framework of &#8220;Katie-vision&#8221; that emulates the zany style of her wacky homemade films starring Monchi, the bulge-eyed pug. There are even mentions of changes made to the movie as it went through various stages of development, from losing a sequence where the family had to kidnap the President of the United States (Barack Obama at the time) to one of the early titles for the movie, which was <em>Control Alt Escape</em>. Plus, you get a much better look at images that flash by in the blink of an eye, including digital family photos showing the years that the Mitchells have spent together.</p>\n<p>In fact, one of the more fascinating changes in development reveals that there was once an action-packed finale that involved a massive PAL-controlled mech made up of computers, cars, slot machines, appliances, construction vehicles, and pretty much any electronic device that could be controlled by the artificial intelligence gone mad. Another take on the massive mech took a more sleek polygonal approach in the style of the PAL headquarters. Not unlike the various character designs for the Mitchell family, there were endless possibilities proposed for this giant machine that didn&#8217;t even make the cut. In fact, a recently released <a href=\"https://twitter.com/billybobmartinz/status/1393299734991802369\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">storyboard sequence of a deleted scene</a> revealed an unused climax where the mech brought back the giant Furby. It&#8217;s crazy how drastically animated movies change throughout production.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-671946 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvstemachines-artbook-katiesroom-700x716.jpg\" alt=\"The Art of The Mitchells vs The Machines\" width=\"700\" height=\"716\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvstemachines-artbook-katiesroom.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/mitchellsvstemachines-artbook-katiesroom-360x368.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>But I think the best details in <em>The Art of The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em> come from the careful attention to quirky character traits. There are several-page spreads that get up close and personal with these characters and their style, from the explosion of cinema and color in Katie&#8217;s room to the droves of dinosaurs carefully placed around Aaron&#8217;s. There&#8217;s also a special focus on the kind of stuff you&#8217;d never even think about while watching the movie. For example, Katie&#8217;s fingers were given an especially irregular and squishy design and careful attention was paid to how she holds things like her cell phone and camera. Aaron&#8217;s hair tuft could never cover both of his eyebrows, and stray hairs should always be sticking out the back. Even Rick&#8217;s beefy anatomy was broken down in great detail to figure out how to best move him as a character.</p>\n<p>For fans of <em>The Art of The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em>, this is a fascinating deep dive into the creation of one of the most visually engaging and endearing movies in recent memory. For you aspiring animators out there, let this serve as a guide to the endless work that goes into creating animation that serves both story and style. And maybe you&#8217;ll walk away with a little inspiration to color outside the lines, whether that&#8217;s on a sketch pad, computer tablet, or just in your everyday life.</p>\n<p><em>The Art of The Mitchells vs. The Machines</em> is <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/1419747495/?tag=film-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">available for purchase today</a>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-art-of-the-mitchells-vs-the-machines-book-review/\">&#8216;The Art of The Mitchells vs. The Machines&#8217; is Packed with Dazzling Illustrations, Animation Insights &#038; More</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"The Largest Marvel LEGO Set Ever Unleashes Spider-Man’s Villains on the Daily Bugle","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=671787","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-671808 aligncenter\" Spider-Man</strong> fan, hopefully you have some money saved up to get your hands on the largest Marvel LEGO set that the building brick company has ever released.</p>\n<p>The LEGO Group has revealed a Daily Bugle LEGO set, a massive scene featuring a bunch of Spider-Man&#8217;s most infamous foes attacking the newspaper office as Peter Parker&#8217;s co-workers are hard at work publishing the latest photos of the webslinger. This is one of the coolest comic book LEGO sets we&#8217;ve ever seen.<span id=\"more-671787\"></span></p>\n<h2>The Daily Bugle LEGO Set</h2>\n\n<a 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n\n\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/daily-bugle-spider-man-lego-set/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-open-front/'><img width=\"241\" https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-open-panelsremoved.jpg 509w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 249px) 100vw, 249px\" /></a>\n\n<p>Standing nearly three-feet tall and comprised of 3,772 pieces, the Daily Bugle LEGO set features the newspaper&#8217;s skyscraper and over two dozen Spider-Man characters. There are super villains swarming the building&#8217;s exterior while the Bugle&#8217;s employees work away in the office interiors.</p>\n\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/daily-bugle-spider-man-lego-set/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-jamesonoffice/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"247\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-jamesonoffice-360x247.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"The Daily Bugle Spider-Man LEGO Set\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-jamesonoffice-360x247.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-jamesonoffice.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n<a srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-bullpen-360x247.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-bullpen.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/daily-bugle-spider-man-lego-set/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-parkeroffice/'><img width=\"360\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-goblin-explosion-360x247.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"The Daily Bugle Spider-Man LEGO Set\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-goblin-explosion-360x247.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-goblin-explosion.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n\n<p>Attacking The Daily Bugle outside is an army of Spider-Man&#8217;s most recognizable villains, from Doc Ock to Venom. Plus, Peter Parker isn&#8217;t the only webslinging superhero hanging around The Daily Bugle. Miles Morales, Spider-Gwen (Ghost Spider), and Spider-Ham are included in the set. Here&#8217;s a look at all the minifigures included with The Daily Bugle LEGO set (via <a href=\"https://www.brothers-brick.com/2021/05/17/lego-marvel-spider-man-76178-daily-bugle-part-2-the-minifigures-review/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Brothers Brick</a>):</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-671805 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-minifigures-700x394.jpg\" alt=\"The Daily Bugle Spider-Man LEGO Set\" width=\"700\" height=\"394\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-minifigures.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-legoset-dailybugle-minifigures-360x203.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Spider-Man</li>\n<li>Miles Morales</li>\n<li>Ghost-Spider</li>\n<li>Spider-Ham</li>\n<li>The Punisher</li>\n<li>Daredevil</li>\n<li>Mysterio</li>\n<li>Blade</li>\n<li>Doctor Octopus</li>\n<li>Venom</li>\n<li>Carnage</li>\n<li>Green Goblin</li>\n<li>Sandman</li>\n<li>Black Cat</li>\n<li>Firestar</li>\n<li>Peter Parker</li>\n<li>Aunt May</li>\n<li>Gwen Stacy</li>\n<li>Betty Brant</li>\n<li>J. Jonah Jameson</li>\n<li>Ben Urich</li>\n<li>Robbie Robertson</li>\n<li>Ron Barney,</li>\n<li>Bernie the Cab Driver</li>\n<li>Amber Grant</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The fact that this is a complete version of The Daily Bugle rather than just a facade with an open back is incredible. You can have the skyscraper completely enclosed, or you can take the panels off to reveal the offices inside, including the angry J. Jonah Jameson, who surely wants more photos of Spider-Man. Sure, the building itself may not match up with the structures of the LEGO Expert Creator buildings out there, but it&#8217;s still extremely cool.</p>\n<p>There are a lot of fun details sprinkled throughout The Daily Bugle LEGO set, including a little framed picture of Spider-Man in Peter Parker&#8217;s office that&#8217;s clearly callback to the classic animated series from the 1960s. Plus, I love the battle details like Green Goblin blasting away part of the building. And there are over a dozen different newspapers in various places over the playset.</p>\n<p>Of course, there&#8217;s always the bad news of the pricetag. The Daily Bugle LEGO set <a href=\"https://www.lego.com/en-us/product/daily-bugle-76178\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">will cost you $299.99</a>. It&#8217;ll go on sale starting on <strong>June 1</strong> at The LEGO Shop online and at LEGO retail stores.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"The Quarantine Stream: ‘Greenland’ is Not Your Typical Disaster Movie","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=672128","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/quarantine-stream-greenland.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-672133\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/quarantine-stream-greenland-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"quarantine stream greenland\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/quarantine-stream-greenland-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/quarantine-stream-greenland-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/quarantine-stream-greenland-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/quarantine-stream-greenland.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><em>(Welcome to <a href=\"https://slashfilm.com/tag/the-quarantine-stream\"><strong>The Quarantine Stream</strong></a>, a series where the /Film team shares what they&#8217;ve been watching while social distancing during the COVID-19 pandemic.)</em></p>\n<p><strong>The Movie:</strong><em> Greenland</em></p>\n<p><strong>Where You Can Stream It:</strong> HBO Max</p>\n<p><strong>The Pitch: </strong>It&#8217;s the end of the world as we know it and <strong>Gerad Butler</strong> does not feel fine.</p>\n<p><strong>Why It&#8217;s Essential Quarantine Viewing: </strong>When <strong><em>Greenland</em> </strong>came out last year, I didn&#8217;t pay it much mind due to both preconceived notions and willful ignorance. I knew it was a disaster movie about a comet hurtling toward Earth, and I knew it starred Gerard Butler. &#8220;Ah,&#8221; I thought. &#8220;That&#8217;ll be dumb!&#8221; Not dumb in a bad way, mind you. But dumb in a way that didn&#8217;t inspire me to rush to see it. But I&#8217;m always the first to admit when I&#8217;m wrong, and I was wrong here. <em>Greenland</em> is not what you expect.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-672128\"></span></p>\n<p>Yes, it&#8217;s a movie about a deadly comet and it does star Gerard Butler. But this isn&#8217;t a mindless disaster pic where Gerard Butler engages in mindless action. Instead, <em>Greenland</em> is a harrowing, often highly disturbing movie that tries to show what would <em>really</em> happen if a comet was headed towards Earth. There are one or two shots of disaster here, but this is not the type of movie that shows us CGI renditions of famous landmarks toppling over. Instead, it&#8217;s about a race against time.</p>\n<p>Butler plays a structural engineer living a normal life with his wife (<strong>Morena Baccarin</strong>) and son (<strong>Roger Dale Floyd</strong>). There&#8217;s a comet headed towards the planet, but no one is really concerned, because all the experts are saying it&#8217;ll crash into the ocean (I was reminded of this movie recently when there was a lot of talk about the Chinese Long March-5b rocket headed toward Earth; experts said that, too, would land in the ocean – and it did. But&#8230;what if it didn&#8217;t?).</p>\n<p>As you can probably guess, the predictions are wrong, and the comet doesn&#8217;t hit the ocean. Instead, it crashes into Tampa, Florida and kills lots of people. And that&#8217;s just the beginning – there are more comets headed towards us, and they&#8217;re going to bring about an extinction-level event. But the government has been planning for this, and they&#8217;ve selected groups of people to hunker down in a bunker in Greenland. Since Butler&#8217;s character is an engineer, he&#8217;s one of the folks chosen to survive – to help rebuild the planet.</p>\n<p>Butler and his family attempt to get on one of the planes flying off to Greenland, but a series of events prevent them from doing so. Now, they have to find a way to get to Greenland on their own before the last of the comets hit. <em>Greenland</em> uses this as a springboard for a series of nail-biting, anxiety-inducing set pieces in which Butler and his family keep running into problems as they try to survive. It&#8217;s incredibly tense, and often quite disturbing. This is not the mindless escapism of a Roland Emmerich disaster pic. It&#8217;s far more chilling – and realistic. And that&#8217;s what gives <em>Greenland</em> its power.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-quarantine-stream-greenland/\">The Quarantine Stream: &#8216;Greenland&#8217; is Not Your Typical Disaster Movie</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Robinson","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=672019","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-hunger-remake.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-672032\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-hunger-remake-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"the hunger remake\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-hunger-remake-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-hunger-remake-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-hunger-remake-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-hunger-remake.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>Angela Robinson</strong>, director of the excellent and underseen <em>Professor Marston and the Wonder Women</em>, is in talks to helm a remake of Tony Scott&#8217;s stylish, sexy vampire film <strong><em>The Hunger</em></strong>. The original starred Catherine Deneuve, David Bowie, and Susan Sarandon, and followed an ancient female vampire who seeks a new lover after losing her longtime companion. <em>American Horror Story</em> and <em>A Simple Favor </em>writer <strong>Jessica Sharzer</strong> is handling the screenplay for the remake.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-672019\"></span></p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"555\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/7a6YFwC2zKA?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Deadline is reporting that Angela Robinson will direct <em>The Hunger</em> remake for Warner Bros. The original film, released in 1983, was directed by the late, great Tony Scott, and starred Catherine Deneuve, David Bowie, and Susan Sarandon. Deneuve played Miriam Blaylock, a vampire over 1000 years old who lives in modern-day (well, modern-day for the 1980s) New York with John (Bowie), a cellist Miriam first met in 18th-century France. John isn&#8217;t technically a vampire, but Miriam told him he would have eternal life as her lover. That turns out to not be true, and John suddenly finds himself aging rapidly. Desperate, John turns to gerontologist Dr. Sarah Roberts (Sarandon) for help. Eventually, John ends up in a state of living death, locked away in Miriam&#8217;s attic. Now lonely, Miriam sets her sights on Sarah as her new lover. The film was an adaptation of a novel by Whitley Strieber. Here&#8217;s the book synopsis:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Eternal youth is a wonderful thing for the few who have it, but for Miriam Blaylock, it is a curse – an existence marred by death and sorrow. Because for the everlasting Miriam, everyone she loves withers and dies. Now, haunted by signs of her adoring husband&#8217;s imminent demise, Miriam sets out in search of a new partner, one who can quench her thirst for love and withstand the test of time. She finds it in the beautiful Sarah Roberts, a brilliant young scientist who may hold the secret to immortality. But one thing stands between the intoxicating Miriam Blaylock and the object of her desire: Dr. Tom Haver&#8230;and he&#8217;s about to realize that love and death to hand in hand.</p></blockquote>\n<p><em>The Hunger</em> wasn&#8217;t really a big hit when it opened but it gained a cult following thanks to its moody, sexy style. While I&#8217;m not sure anyone can recreate Scott&#8217;s visual flair, I&#8217;m a big fan of Angela Robinson&#8217;s <em>Professor Marston and the Wonder Women</em>, a sexy, sweet movie about the creator of Wonder Woman and the long-running polyamorous relationship he enjoyed with his wife and one of his students. That film was criminally underseen, and Robinson hasn&#8217;t helmed a film since its 2017 release. <em>The Hunger</em> remake will be scripted by Jessica Sharzer, who wrote the surprisingly good dark comedy <em>A Simple Favor</em>. Berlanti Schechter&#8217;s Greg Berlanti and Sarah Schechter will produce.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-hunger-remake/\">&#8216;The Hunger&#8217; Remake Coming From &#8216;Professor Marston and the Wonder Women&#8217; Director Angela Robinson</a> appeared first on <a 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"‘Stand By Me’ Returning to Theaters For 35th Anniversary","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=671918","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Stand-By-Me-Returning-to-Theaters.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-671926\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong><em>Stand By Me</em></strong>, the<strong> Rob Reiner</strong> movie based on <strong>Stephen King</strong>&#8216;s novella &#8220;The Body,&#8221; is headed back to the big screen to mark the movie&#8217;s 35th anniversary. The screenings will feature the bonus featurette &#8220;Walking the Tracks: The Summer of Stand by Me,&#8221; which follows &#8220;Stephen King as he recalls what led him to write the stories of his childhood, how they impacted the development of the movie, and Rob Reiner as he reminisces about the casting of the four leads.&#8221; Screenings will take place in theaters nationwide on <strong>May 23</strong> and <strong>May 26</strong>.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-671918\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>Stand By Me Returning to Theaters</strong></h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/FidWnmtO8eE?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>One of the very best Stephen King adaptations is <em>Stand By Me</em>, a funny, emotional coming-of-age flick that stars <strong>Wil Wheaton</strong>, <strong>River Phoenix</strong>, <strong>Corey Feldman</strong>, <strong>Jerry O&#8217;Connell</strong>, and <strong>Kiefer Sutherland</strong>. The film follows &#8220;four boys on a two-day journey. In a treehouse at the edge of Castle Rock, a small, woodsy Oregon town, a budding 12-year-old writer named Gordie LaChance (Wheaton) is about to begin an extraordinary trek into the heart of the northwestern forest, an experience that will alter the course of his life forever. His best friend Vern (O&#8217;Connell) has overheard his older brother and a friend talking about their discovery of a dead body in the woods. Hoping they can get credit for finding the body, Gordie sets off with insecure, frightened Vern, tough guy Chris (Phoenix), and daredevil Teddy (Feldman) on an adventure that becomes an odyssey of self-discovery. Their journey begins innocently with a dream of becoming town heroes, but before it is over, Gordie, Chris, Teddy, and Vern will be tested in ways they had never imagined.&#8221;</p>\n<p>As a director, Rob Reiner can be very hit or miss, but his two Stephen King adaptations – <em>Stand By Me</em> and <em>Misery</em> – are both pretty damn great. King himself once said he thought <em>Stand By Me</em> was the best film based on his work (although he seems to change his mind on that from time to time). &#8220;&#8221;I thought it was true to the book, and because it had the emotional gradient of the story. It was moving,&#8221; King previously <a href=\"http://www.rollingstone.com/culture/features/stephen-king-the-rolling-stone-interview-20141031\">said</a>. &#8220;I think I scared &#8230; (director) Rob Reiner. He showed it to me in the screening room at the Beverly Hills Hotel. &#8230; And you have to remember that the movie was made on a shoestring. It was supposed to be one of those things that opened in six theaters and then maybe disappeared. And instead it went viral. When the movie was over, I hugged him because I was moved to tears, because it was so autobiographical.&#8221;</p>\n<p>And now Reiner&#8217;s <em>Stand By Me</em> is headed back to the big screen to mark the movie&#8217;s 35th anniversary. The film will screen in select movie theaters nationwide on Sunday, May 23 at 3:00 P.M. and 7:00 P.M.,  and Wednesday, May 26 at 7:00 P.M. (all times local). Screenings will include the featurette &#8220;Walking the Tracks: The Summer of Stand by Me,&#8221; where Stephen King &#8220;recalls what led him to write the stories of his childhood, how they impacted the development of the movie, and Rob Reiner&#8230;reminisces about the casting of the four leads.&#8221; Tickets are available <a href=\"https://ymlptr3.net/52c8bmbqubqadaewuwsaiawshapaybwby/click.php\">here</a>.</p>\n<div>\n<div></div>\n</div>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/stand-by-me-returning-to-theaters/\">&#8216;Stand By Me&#8217; Returning to Theaters For 35th Anniversary</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" Series","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=671849","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-671857\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/master-of-none-2-700x299.jpg\" alt=\"master of none season 3\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/master-of-none-2-768x328.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/master-of-none-2.jpg 1113w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong><em>Master of None</em></strong><em> </em>has already mastered its brand of comedy-drama with its first two seasons, so why not change things up in a major way with its long-awaited season 3? The third season which comes nearly four years after season 2 aired on Netflix, goes by the title <strong><em>Master of None Presents: Moments in Love</em></strong>, and appears to take that title to heart. A small-scale, low-key affair that shifts the focus to<strong> Lena Waithe</strong>&#8216;s Denise and her life with her wife Alicia (BAFTA winner <strong>Naomi Ackie</strong>), <em>Master of None</em> looks more intimate than anything the show has done before. See <strong>Aziz Ansari</strong>, <strong>Alan Yang</strong>, Waithe, Ackie, and others go behind the scenes in the <em>Master of None</em> special look below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-671849\"></span></p>\n<h2>Master of None Season 3 Special Look</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/hv-cOEmVXds?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p><em>Master of None</em> season 3 was sprung upon us by surprise, with Netflix first giving update earlier this year that the series would be <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/master-of-none-season-3-confirmed/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">returning for a third season</a> before a season 3 trailer was just as suddenly dropped. Now, we&#8217;re less than a week away from the show&#8217;s premiere, and Netflix is granting another special look at the series, in a making-of featurette that goes into how the show was made under COVID-19 restrictions, on a single soundstage, with a small crew. The result is something that looks small, intimate, and ultimately very lovely.</p>\n<p>&#8220;On paper, everything sounds like a terrible idea,&#8221; Ansari says in the featurette. &#8220;Oh, I&#8217;m not going to be in the show anymore? We&#8217;re just going to just hold on them doing laundry for three minutes? It was a little bit scary, because it was nothing we&#8217;d done before. But the first time we read it, where it wasn&#8217;t like me reading with Lena, it was another woman, [we thought], &#8216;Whoa this is going to work, this is cool.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Waithe and Ansari pen the entire five-episode season, and Ansari directing each episode. Here is the synopsis for <em>Master of None</em> season 3:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The Emmy Award-winning MASTER OF NONE returns with a new season that chronicles the relationship of Denise (Emmy Award winner Lena Waithe) and her partner Alicia (BAFTA winner Naomi Ackie). Directed by series co-creator and Emmy winner Aziz Ansari, and scripted by Ansari and Waithe, this new season is a modern love story that intimately illustrates the ups and downs of marriage, struggles with fertility, and personal growth both together and apart. Fleeting romantic highs meet crushing personal losses while existential questions of love and living are raised. Co-created by Ansari and Emmy Award winner Alan Yang, Season 3 delivers an evolution of the series that remains tethered to previous seasons while breaking new storytelling ground of its own.</p></blockquote>\n<p><em>Master of None</em> season 3 debuts on Netflix Sunday, <strong>May 23, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/leslie-odom-jr-e1621364931361.jpeg 1536w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Rian Johnson</strong> is not throwing away his shot at assembling the best ensemble for a murder mystery movie. And he&#8217;s doing pretty good so far with his highly anticipated sequel <strong><em>Knives Out 2</em></strong>, which has now recruited <strong>Leslie Odom Jr.</strong> to the cast.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-672072\"></span></p>\n<p>Fresh off his Oscar nomination for his role in <em>One Night in Miami</em>, Leslie Odom Jr. has already landed his next gig as part of the star-studded cast for Rian Johnson&#8217;s <em>Knives Out</em> sequel. <a href=\"https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/movies/movie-news/leslie-odom-jr-knives-out-sequel-1234954701/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Hollywood Reporter</a> broke the news that Odom Jr. will be joining the <strong>Daniel Craig</strong>-led <em>Knives Out 2</em> cast, alongside fellow franchise newcomers <strong>Kathryn Hahn</strong>, <strong>Janelle Monáe</strong>, <strong>Dave Bautista</strong>, and <strong>Edward Norton</strong>.</p>\n<p>Plot details and characters are being kept under lock and key for now, but right now <em>Knives Out 2</em> is gunning for the first movie&#8217;s title as the best-cast mystery movie&#8230;ever? Like the first film, Johnson has assembled a murderer&#8217;s row of actors, and Odom Jr. is no exception. The breakout star of Broadway&#8217;s <em>Hamilton</em>, Odom Jr. has steadily worked at carving out a name for himself on the big screen and received an Oscar nomination for playing Same Cooke in last year&#8217;s <em>One Night in Miami</em>. It&#8217;s not Odom Jr.&#8217;s first time being part of a star-studded whodunit either. He also starred in Kenneth Branagh&#8217;s 2017 mystery film <em>Murder on the Orient Express</em>, which brings him full circle on the Agatha Christie-inspired whodunits.</p>\n<p>Last week, we got a new casting announcement for <em>Knives Out 2</em> nearly every day, and it seems like this week will keep the momentum going. We&#8217;ll likely learn more cast additions as the film prepares to start shooting soon in Greece.</p>\n<p>Rian Johnson is back to direct the sequel as part of a massive deal he signed with Netflix to make both <em>Knives Out 2</em> and <em>Knives Out 3. </em>The deal landed Johnson and producing partner Ram Bergman, under their T-Street banner, $469 million for the two sequels, with the stipulation that “Craig must star in the sequels and that each must have at least the budget of the 2019 movie, which was in the $40 million range.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The first <em>Knives Out</em> was a massive hit when it hit theaters in 2018, raking in $311.4 million at the box office on a $40 million budget and earning acclaim for the phenomenal performances and the razor-sharp writing. If the sequel and its buzzy cast can manage to match the first film&#8217;s sense of fun and mystery (as well as allow Craig to go bananas with his Southern fried accent), then it will be undoubtedly one of the most exciting movies of the year.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/leslie-odom-jr-knives-out-2-cast/\">&#8216;Knives Out 2&#8217; Adds sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Steve Martin</strong> and <strong>Martin Short</strong> are comedy legends whose decades-spanning friendship has been going on for almost as long as their absence from the screen (barring the occasional <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/steve-martin-and-martin-short-netflix-special-trailer/\">stand-up special</a>). So it must take something good to bring them back in front of the cameras together. Martin and Short star opposite <strong>Selena Gomez</strong> in <strong><em>Only Murders in the Building</em></strong>, a new mystery-comedy series coming from Hulu. Watch the <em>Only Murders in the Building</em> trailer below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-672030\"></span></p>\n<h2>Only Murders in the Building Trailer</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/Lxg1y4x4jWM?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Hulu&#8217;s trailer for <em>Only Murders in the Building</em> teases the absurd tone of the series and the release date, which is set for August 31. It&#8217;s a long time to keep us waiting for the Martin and Short reunion, but you can&#8217;t blame Hulu for keeping us in suspense. The series looks like a heightened and stylish comedy series that taps into Martin and Short&#8217;s goofy brand of humor, while appealing to the young-un&#8217;s with Gomez, who pulls from her Disney sitcom roots to keep up with the comedy masters. The three of them play a group of true-crime obsessives who investigate the grisly death of a neighbor in their Upper West Side apartment, leading them to bite off more than they can chew.</p>\n<p>Also joining Martin, Short, and Gomez in the cast are <strong>Aaron Dominguez</strong> and <strong>Amy Ryan</strong>. Martin co-wrote and co-created the series alongside <strong>John Hoffman</strong>, who is probably best known for his work on series such as <em>Looking</em> and <em>Grace &#38; Grankie</em>.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s the synopsis for <em>Only Murders in the Building</em>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>From the minds of Steve Martin, Dan Fogelman and John Hoffman comes a comedic murder-mystery series for the ages. &#8220;Only Murders in the Building&#8221; follows three strangers (Steve Martin, Martin Short and Selena Gomez) who share an obsession with true crime and suddenly find themselves wrapped up in one. When a grisly death occurs inside their exclusive Upper West Side apartment building, the trio suspects murder and employs their precise knowledge of true crime to investigate the truth. As they record a podcast of their own to document the case, the three unravel the complex secrets of the building which stretch back years. Perhaps even more explosive are the lies they tell one another. Soon, the endangered trio comes to realize a killer might be living amongst them as they race to decipher the mounting clues before it’s too late.</p></blockquote>\n<p><em>Only Murders in the</em> <em>Building</em> arrives on Hulu on <strong>August 31, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/only-murders-in-the-building-trailer/\">&#8216;Only Murders in the Building&#8217; Trailer: Steve Martin, Martin Short, and Selena Gomez Find Out Whodunit in This New Hulu Series</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" Chippendales","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=672035","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Immigrant-Series-Kumail-Nanjiani.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-672057\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Immigrant-Series-Kumail-Nanjiani-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"Immigrant Series Kumail Nanjiani\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Immigrant-Series-Kumail-Nanjiani-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Immigrant-Series-Kumail-Nanjiani-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Immigrant-Series-Kumail-Nanjiani-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Immigrant-Series-Kumail-Nanjiani.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>Kumail Nanjiani</strong> is using his recently acquired swole-ness to star in the Hulu limited series <strong><em>Immigrant</em></strong>. Nanjiani will play Somen &#8220;Steve&#8221; Banerjee, the creator of the male stripper dance troupe Chippendales. Chippendales rocketed Banerjee to fame and fortune, but he also was later caught up in a criminal scandal and went on to plead guilty to attempted arson, racketeering, and murder for hire.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-672035\"></span></p>\n<p>Hulu has given a straight-to-series order for <em>Immigrant</em>, an 8-episode limited series created by <strong>Robert Siegel</strong> and executive produced by and starring Kumail Nanjiani. The series is based on the &#8220;true story of Somen &#8216;Steve&#8217; Banerjee (played by Nanjiani), the Indian-American entrepreneur who started Chippendales. The series will detail the insane, darkly comedic, crime-ridden story behind the unique male revue that became a cultural phenomenon.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Banerjee emigrated from India to Los Angeles with dreams of fame and fortune. He found it with the creation of Chippendales, a dance troupe of male exocit dancers. Soon he was pulling in $8 million a year – but it would eventually all come crashing down due to a series of criminal activities. <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somen_Banerjee\">Wikipedia</a> has some more info on that:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Banerjee was later charged with having enlisted the aid of Ray Colon, in 1990 and 1991, to help carry out a plot to kill Michael Fullington, a former Chippendales dancer and choreographer, and two other ex-Chippendales dancers, who Banerjee felt were competition to the Chippendales franchise. He was also indicted for allegedly orchestrating the 1987 murder of his former choreographer/added partner Nick De Noia. It was also alleged that it was his intent to also have Nahin murdered. He eventually pleaded guilty to attempted arson, racketeering, and murder for hire. He entered into a plea agreement that would have led to 26 years in prison, loss of his share of the Chippendales’ parent company (Nahin retaining his share), and most of his estate.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Hulu&#8217;s <em>Immigrant</em> will be written by Robert Siegel and executive produced by Siegel, Nanjiani, Dylan Sellers, and Emily V. Gordon as well as Rajiv Joseph and Mehar Sethi who will also write on the series.</p>\n<p>Interestingly enough, <em>Immigrant</em> isn&#8217;t the only project about Banerjee in the works. In 2020 it was <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/chippendales-murder-movie/\">announced</a> that <em>I, Tonya</em> and <em>Cruella</em> director Craig Gillespie would direct a movie about the Chippendales founder, with Dev Patel playing the role. However, there&#8217;s been almost no news about that since the announcement, so it&#8217;s unclear if it&#8217;s still moving forward at this point.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=MAvRpD6t5jI:ZCFaD6Tic_o:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"Charles Grodin, Star of ‘The Heartbreak Kid’, ‘Beethoven’, ‘Midnight Run’, and More, Has Died at 86","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=672046","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-672054 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Charles-Grodin-dead-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Charles Grodin dead\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Charles-Grodin-dead.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Charles-Grodin-dead-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Charles Grodin</strong>, the actor who appeared in the <em>Beethoven</em> films, <em>Midnight Run</em>, <em>The Heartbreak Kid</em>, and <em>The Great Muppet Caper</em>, to name just a few credits, has passed away at the age of 86. Grodin&#8217;s son told <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/18/movies/charles-grodin-dead.html?smid=tw-nytimesarts&#38;smtyp=cur\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The New York Times</a> that his father&#8217;s cause of death was bone marrow cancer.<span id=\"more-672046\"></span></p>\n<p>After starting his career with an uncredited role in Disney&#8217;s <em>20,000 Leagues Under the Sea</em> in the mid-1950s, Grodin dropped out of college to pursue acting, writing, and directing for the stage, appearing in several Broadway productions and directing multiple Broadway shows as well. He developed the kind of All-American good looks which made him a versatile cinematic asset during the latter half of the twentieth century, and always appeared to be equally comfortable in supporting roles as leading ones. Grodin was one of those actors who made everything he did look easy, and he was especially adept at playing guys who got in over their heads. His deadpan comedic reactions and ability to portray put-upon or frustrated characters made him stand out from his contemporaries, and he was a guy I was always personally delighted to see pop up in any capacity whatsoever – even in a brief cameo in <em>So I Married an Axe Murderer</em>.</p>\n<p>As his Hollywood career began, Grodin chipped his way through small roles in popular television shows like <em>The F.B.I.</em> and <em>The Virginian</em>, and then played Dr. Hill in Roman Polanski&#8217;s horror classic <em>Rosemary&#8217;s Baby</em>. He then worked with the acclaimed comedy duo of Nichols and May, appearing in Mike Nichols&#8217; 1970 adaptation of <em>Catch-22</em> and later starring as Lenny Cantrow in Elaine May&#8217;s 1972 comedy <em>The Heartbreak Kid</em>, in which he played a total scumbag who ditches his wife for a younger blonde. That character should be completely irredeemable on the page, but through his excellent performance, Grodin somehow manages to grasp onto the tiniest bit of the audience&#8217;s sympathy.</p>\n<p>Roles in films like the <em>King Kong</em> remake, <em>Heaven Can Wait</em>, and <em>The Incredible Shrinking Woman</em> followed, as well as a memorable turn as the over-the-top villain in 1981&#8217;s <em>The Great Muppet Caper</em>, which is a terrific, scenery-chewing performance that doesn&#8217;t get the credit it deserves for the way it walks the perfect tonal high wire without missing a beat. <em>The Woman in Red</em> and <em>Ishtar</em> are a couple of other notable credits for him on the way to <em>Midnight Run</em>, which pitted Grodin against Robert De Niro and which became a beloved cross-country buddy movie staple.</p>\n<p>That gave way to the next stage of his career, where he perfected the &#8220;put-upon dad&#8221; archetype and introduced himself to a whole new generation in movies like <em>Beethoven</em>, <em>Beethoven&#8217;s 2nd</em>, and <em>Clifford</em>. There was a 12 year period between the mid-90s and the mid-2000s where he didn&#8217;t appear in anything, but then his career picked back up again with appearances in <em>The Ex</em>, <em>The Humbling</em>, Noah Baumbach&#8217;s <em>While We&#8217;re Young</em>, the FX series <em>Louie</em>, the <em>Madoff</em> miniseries, and more.</p>\n<p>Rest in peace, Mr. Grodin – you will be deeply missed.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/charles-grodin-dead/\">Charles Grodin, Star of &#8216;The Heartbreak Kid&#8217;, &#8216;Beethoven&#8217;, &#8216;Midnight Run&#8217;, and More, Has Died at 86</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Screen","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=672016","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-672021\" /></p>\n<p><strong><em>Dear Evan Hansen</em></strong> has made it to the big screen. A musical sensation when it debuted on Broadway in 2015, the Tony-winning musical now gets the feature film treatment with original star <strong>Ben Platt</strong> back in his blue polo, and looking a little rough for a teenager. Watch the <em>Dear Evan Hansen</em> trailer below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-672016\"></span></p>\n<h2>Dear Evan Hansen Trailer</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/g_c_Jd-hP-s?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Directed by<strong> Stephen Chbosky</strong> <em>(The Perks of Being A Wallflower</em>, <em>Wonder</em>), <em>Dear Evan Hansen</em> follows a teenage boy with social anxiety (Platt) who is tasked with writing encouraging letters to himself by his therapist. But when one of those letters ends up in the pocket of a fellow student who commits suicide, Evan Hansen ends up caught in a lie that finally affords him all the friends and affection he&#8217;d been craving — but at the cost of pretending to be someone he&#8217;s not.</p>\n<p><em>Dear Evan Hansen</em> was a deeply polarizing musical when it debuted in 2015 for exactly the reasons you probably think, having just read that premise. But despite the criticisms over its story, <em>Dear Evan Hansen</em> went on to win six Tony Awards, including Best Actor for Platt, who reprises the role of the teenaged Evan Hansen at a fresh-faced 27 (please free this man from playing high schoolers for the rest of his life, he got so close with <em>Pitch Perfect</em>). But regardless what you think of the musical, it&#8217;s undeniably got some good songs, composed by the Tony-winning songwriting team <strong>Benj Pasek &#38; Justin Paul</strong>, the hit makers behind the songs from <em>La La Land</em> and <em>The Greatest Showman.</em> The Tony-winning writer <strong>Steven Levenson</strong> also adapts the book for the screen.</p>\n<p><em>Dear Evan Hansen</em> stars <strong>Amy Adams</strong>, <strong>Julianne Moore</strong>, <strong>Kaitlyn Dever</strong> (<em>Booksmart</em>), <strong>Amandla Stenberg</strong> (<em>The Hate U Give</em>), <strong>Colton Ryan</strong> (Apple TV+’s <em>Little Voice)</em>, <strong>Nik Dodani</strong> (Netflix’s <em>Atypical</em>), <strong>DeMarius Copes</strong> (Broadway’s <em>Mean Girls</em>), and <strong>Danny Pino</strong> (<em>Law &#38; Order: Special Victims Unit</em>). It&#8217;s produced by Marc Platt (<em>La La Land, Into the Woods, Mary Poppins Returns</em>) and Adam Siegel (<em>2 Guns, Drive</em>), and is executive produced by Michael Bederman, Steven Levenson, Benj Pasek and Justin Paul.</p>\n<p>Here is the synopsis for <em>Dear Evan Hansen</em>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The breathtaking, generation-defining Broadway phenomenon becomes a soaring cinematic event as Tony, Grammy and Emmy Award winner Ben Platt reprises his role as an anxious, isolated high schooler aching for understanding and belonging amid the chaos and cruelty of the social-media age.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Universal has set <em>Dear Evan Hansen</em> to open in theaters <strong>September 24, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>There&#8217;s a long cinematic tradition of comedians making movies based on events in their own lives, from Woody Allen to Judd Apatow. Now we can add <strong>Iliza Shlesinger</strong> to that group, because she has written and stars in a new movie called <em><strong>Good on Paper</strong></em> that&#8217;s &#8220;based on a mostly true story&#8221; about a boyfriend she had (played by <em>Veronica Mars</em> actor <strong>Ryan Hansen</strong>) who may not be exactly who he appears. It definitely seems as if she&#8217;s following in Amy Schumer&#8217;s footsteps here, transitioning from stage persona to actress while writing a vehicle for herself to star in like Schumer did with 2015&#8217;s <em>Trainwreck</em>. Shlesinger has a comfortable relationship with Netflix already, having released five comedy specials and a sketch show and appeared in Netflix originals like <em>Girlboss</em>, <em>Pieces of a Woman</em>, and <em>Spenser Confidential</em>, so this feels like a natural home for her.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Ryan Hansen broke out playing the lovable jerk Dick Casablancas on <em>Veronica Mars</em>, and he parlayed that into a role in the ensemble of another beloved TV series, the cancelled-too-soon Starz comedy <em>Party Down</em>. (Fun fact: <em>Party Down</em> is <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/party-down-revival-starz/\">getting a revival</a>, although last we heard, it wasn&#8217;t clear which actors were returning for it.)</p>\n<p><strong>Kimmy Gatewood</strong> is directing this film, which will be her feature debut after directing tons of television, including shows like The CW&#8217;s <em>Crazy Ex-Girlfriend</em>, Netflix&#8217;s <em>The Baby-Sitter&#8217;s Club</em> revival, and the Peacock original comedy series <em>Girls5eva</em>. Veteran comedian <strong>Margaret Cho</strong> (<em>Drop Dead Diva</em>) and actress <strong>Rebecca Rittenhouse</strong> (<em>Unfriended: Dark Web</em>, <em>Once Upon a Time in Hollywood</em>) round out the rest of the film&#8217;s cast.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s the official synopsis for <em>Good on Paper</em>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Andrea Singer always put her stand-up career first, and while dating came easy, love wasn&#8217;t a priority&#8230; that is until she meets Dennis, a quirky nerd with disarming charm who coaxes her into letting her guard down. Her best friend Margot isn’t convinced he’s all he seems and she urges Andrea to embark on a wild goose chase to uncover who Dennis really is. Based on a mostly true story, GOOD ON PAPER is written by and stars the hilariously sharp-witted Iliza Shlesinger. Also starring Ryan Hansen, Margaret Cho, and Rebecca Rittenhouse.</p></blockquote>\n<p><em>Good on Paper</em> will be available to stream on Netflix starting <strong>June 23</strong>, 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Liam Neeson</strong> movie characters have faced some pretty extreme challenges over the past decade or so: a missing daughter, surviving a plane crash, releasing the Now he&#8217;s facing off against the only foe that he may be able to beat temporarily, but that is sure to get the best of him in the end: time.</p>\n<p>In <strong><em>The Ice Road</em></strong>, Neeson plays a big rig driver who has experience driving on the dangerous icy roads of Canada. When a mine collapses and the trapped workers running out of time, Neeson and co-star <strong>Laurence Fishburne</strong> have to put a team of specialists together to traverse that treacherous terrain and save the day. So yeah, it&#8217;s essentially Neeson doing a riff on <em>Armageddon</em> – and this project hails from one of the writers of that movie, so it feels like more than just a coincidence.<span id=\"more-672031\"></span></p>\n<h2>The Ice Road Trailer</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/-zjikObAJHk?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p><strong>Jonathan Hensleigh</strong> wrote and directed this icy action thriller, which should appeal to the wide swath of Neeson-loving dads out there as well as the folks who have seen every episode of the reality TV series <em>Ice Road Truckers</em>. And yes, Hensleigh is one of the credited writers of <em>Armageddon</em>, alongside names like Robert Roy Pool (<em>Outbreak</em>), Shane Salerno (the upcoming <em>Avatar</em> sequels), Tony Gilroy (<em>The Bourne Legacy</em>), and some guy named J.J. Abrams. But he also wrote the famous spec script <em>Simon Says</em>, which was eventually made as <em>Die Hard with a Vengeance</em>, and wrote the scripts for <em>Jumanji</em> and the Nic Cage film <em>Next</em>, while writing and directing <em>Kill the Irishman</em> and the 2004 adaptation of <em>The Punisher</em>, which starred Thomas Jane in the lead role.</p>\n<p>Netflix has <strong>Benjamin Walker</strong> (<em>Abraham Lincoln: Vampire Hunter</em>), <strong>Amber Midthunder</strong> (<em>Legion</em>), and <strong>Marcus Thomas</strong> (<em>Drowning Mona</em>) listed as additional cast members, but IMDb says <strong>Holt McCallany</strong> (<em>Mindhunter</em>, <em>Lights Out</em>) is also on board, so I&#8217;m curious to see if that ends up being true.</p>\n<p>Here is the film&#8217;s official synopsis:</p>\n<div>\n<blockquote>\n<div>After a remote diamond mine collapses in far northern Canada, a ‘big-rig’ ice road driver (Neeson) must lead an impossible rescue mission over a frozen ocean to save the trapped miners. Contending with thawing waters and a massive storm, they discover the real threat is one they never saw coming.</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<p><em>The Ice Road</em> will be available to stream on Netflix starting <strong>June 25</strong>, <strong>2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-ice-road-trailer/\">&#8216;The Ice Road&#8217; Trailer: It&#8217;s Basically &#8216;Armageddon&#8217; on Ice, Starring Liam Neeson</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 22:55:43","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:43","title":"TV Upfronts: ABC, FOX, and NBC Announce Renewals, Cancellations, and Series Orders, ‘Clarice’ & More Heading to Paramount+","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=672010","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-672022 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/nbc-fox-abc-logos-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"2021 New, Renewed and Canceled TV Shows\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/nbc-fox-abc-logos.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/nbc-fox-abc-logos-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Even though they&#8217;re not quite as celebratory or hyped as usual thanks to the coronavirus pandemic, this year&#8217;s TV upfront presentations are still unfolding this month. So far, NBC, ABC and FOX have revealed series orders and trailers for the new shows coming up for the 2021-2022 season. But with new shows coming in and the reliable ones sticking around, there are plenty of shows that won&#8217;t be coming back for another season. Find out the latest updates from the 2021-2022 TV upfronts presentations below.<span id=\"more-672010\"></span></p>\n<h2>New, Renewed and Canceled TV Shows for 2021-2022</h2>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-416944 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/abc-logo-splash-dark-700x309.jpg\" alt=\"ABC\" width=\"700\" height=\"309\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/abc-logo-splash-dark-700x309.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/abc-logo-splash-dark-360x159.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/abc-logo-splash-dark.jpg 796w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>ABC</h2>\n<p>First up, ABC has announced (via <a href=\"https://www.usatoday.com/story/entertainment/tv/2021/05/14/abc-renews-the-rookie-black-ish-returns-final-season/5093427001/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">USA Today</a>) that <strong><em>The Rookie</em></strong> with <strong>Nathan Fillion</strong>, the ensemble drama <strong><em>A Million Little Things</em></strong>, the <strong><em>Roseanne</em></strong> spin-off <strong><em>The Conners</em></strong>, the freshman series <strong><em>Home Economics</em></strong>, and the flashback comedy series <strong><em>The Goldbergs</em></strong> have all been renewed for another season.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, even though <strong><em>Black-ish</em></strong> has been renewed for an eighth season, it will also be the final season of the family comedy from <strong>Kenya Barris</strong>. On the other side of the spectrum, <a href=\"https://tvline.com/2021/05/10/greys-anatomy-renewed-season-18-ellen-pompeo-contract/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TV Line</a> has news on <strong><em>Grey&#8217;s Anatomy</em></strong> getting picked up for an 18th season, including the return of <strong>Ellen Pompeo</strong>. Plus, the sister series <strong><em>Station 19</em> </strong>is also coming back for a fifth season, so there might be another crossover in store.</p>\n<p class=\"gnt_ar_b_p\">But not all shows can stick around, and unfortunately <a href=\"https://tvline.com/2021/05/14/abc-cancelled-shows-2021-list-mixedish-rebel/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TV Line</a> reports ABC has canceled <strong>Katey Sagal</strong>&#8216;s new series <strong><em>Rebel</em></strong> and the freshman sitcom <strong><em>Call Your Mother</em></strong> starring <strong>Kyra Sedgwick</strong>. Also given the axe were the legal drama <strong><em>For Life</em></strong>, the <em>Black-ish</em> spin-off <strong><em>Mixed-ish</em></strong>, and the family sitcom <strong><em>American Housewife</em></strong>.</p>\n<p>Finally, ABC will be filling the gaps in their schedule with new series orders for <strong><em>The Wonder Years</em> </strong>reboot, a hip-hop themed dramedy called Queens, a workplace comedy set in a Philadelphia public school called <strong><em>Abbott Elementary</em></strong>, and <strong><em>Maggie</em></strong>, a series based on a short film about a psychic who gets a glimpse of her own future, prompting her to change how she lives in the present. You can check out the trailers for all those new shows <a href=\"https://www.thewrap.com/wonder-years-reboot-trailer-new-abc-shows-queens-maggie-abbott-elementary/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">over here</a>.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-544281 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fox-layoffs-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"fox layoffs\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fox-layoffs-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fox-layoffs-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fox-layoffs-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fox-layoffs.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>FOX</h2>\n<p>Over at FOX, <a href=\"https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/tv/tv-news/911-great-north-resident-renewed-fox-1234952128/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Hollywood Reporter</a> confirms the network has actually renewed many of their previous shows, likely knowing they have to fill space in 2022 now that they no longer will be hosting Thursday night NFL games. The rescue drama <strong><em>911</em></strong> is returning for a fifth season and the spin-off <strong><em>911: Lone Star</em></strong> will be back for a third season.</p>\n<p>FOX also renewed <strong><em>The Resident</em></strong> for a fifth season, and they&#8217;ve given an early third season order to the animated comedy <strong><em>The Great North</em></strong>, which was already sticking around for a second season. They join previous renewals for <strong><em>Call Me Kat</em></strong> and animation staples <strong><em>Bob’s Burgers</em></strong>, <strong><em>Family Guy</em></strong>, and <strong><em>The Simpsons</em></strong>, as well as the younger animated comedy <em><strong>Duncanville</strong>. </em></p>\n<p>Unfortunately, that means <strong><em>Prodigal Son</em></strong>, <strong><em>Bless the Harts</em></strong>, and <strong><em>Filthy Rich</em></strong> are being left behind, with all three shows getting canceled.</p>\n<p>As for new shows, FOX has ordered a comedy called <strong><em>Pivoting</em></strong> starring <strong>Eliza Coupe</strong> (<em>Happy Endings</em>), <strong>Ginnifer Goodwin</strong> (<em>Once Upon a Time</em>) and <strong>Maggie Q</strong> (<em>Designated Survivor</em>). The network is also counting on laughs from the comedy <strong><em>Welcome to Flatch</em></strong>, a BBC mockumentary-style series that explores the lives of residents in a small American town, including <strong>Seann William Scott</strong> (<em>American Pie</em>) and <strong>Aya Cash</strong> (<em>The Boys</em>).</p>\n<p>On the drama side, FOX has snagged <strong><em>The Cleaning Lady</em></strong>, where <em>Daredevil</em> co-star <strong>Elodie Yung</strong> becomes a cleaning lady for organized crime, using her cunning and intelligence to forge her own path in the criminal underworld. They&#8217;ve also picked up a dramedy called <strong><em>The Big Leap</em></strong>, which follows a group of diverse, down-on-their-luck characters attempting to change their lives by participating in a potentially life-ruining reality dance show.</p>\n<p>You can check out trailers for all the new FOX shows <a href=\"https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/tv/tv-news/fox-2021-trailers-1234954485/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">over here</a>.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-555045 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/nbc-logo-full-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"NBC\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/nbc-logo-full.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/nbc-logo-full-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>NBC</h2>\n<p>In case you hadn&#8217;t heard, NBC has already renewed their trio of procedurals set in the Windy City with new seasons ordered for <strong><em>Chicago Fire</em></strong>, <strong><em>Chicago P.D.</em></strong>, and <strong><em>Chicago Med</em></strong>. Joining them will be<strong><em> The Blacklist</em></strong> and the continuation of <strong><em>Law &#38; Order: Organized Crime</em></strong> and <strong><em>Law &#38; Order SVU</em></strong>. Dramas <strong><em>New Amsterdam</em></strong> and <strong><em>Transplant</em></strong> will also be coming back.</p>\n<p>On the comedy side of things, freshman shows <strong><em>Kenan</em></strong>, <strong><em>Young Rock</em></strong>, and <em><strong>Mr. Mayor</strong></em> have already been renewed, and all three shows will be getting <a href=\"https://www.comingsoon.net/tv/news/1174017-young-rock-holiday-special-more-ordered\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">their own holiday specials</a> outside of the second seasons that will be arriving in January 2022. Meanwhile, all you <strong><em>Brooklyn Nine-Nine</em></strong> fans waiting for the <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/brooklyn-nine-nine-season-8-2/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">eighth and final season</a> of the show will be happy to hear that it will arrive after this year&#8217;s Summer Olympics.</p>\n<p>NBC&#8217;s hit series <strong><em>This Is Us</em></strong> will also be returning for a sixth season, but <a href=\"https://variety.com/2021/tv/news/this-is-us-end-season-6-1234971587/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Variety</a> reports this will be the last one. This is a planned end to the series that the showrunners have been talking about for awhile, so at least the show will go out on its own terms.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, <strong><em>The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</em></strong> will be sticking around a lot longer with the show getting renewed <a href=\"https://deadline.com/2021/05/the-tonight-show-jimmy-fallon-renewed-at-nbc-for-five-years-1234758368/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">for a whopping five years</a>. So if you like to see Jimmy Fallon hamming it up with your favorite celebrities, pop a bottle of champagne.</p>\n<p>As for <em><strong>Zoey’s Extraordinary Playlist</strong>, <strong>Manifest</strong>, <strong>Debris</strong></em> and <strong><em>Good Girls</em>,</strong> NBC hasn&#8217;t determined what they&#8217;re doing with those shows yet, but they haven&#8217;t been canceled. So fans will just have to be patient.</p>\n<p>When it comes to new shows, NBC isn&#8217;t going too crazy this year. <a href=\"https://tvline.com/2021/05/14/nbc-fall-lineup-2021-law-and-order-thursday-this-is-us-final-season/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TV Line</a> reports they&#8217;ve only ordered the dramas <strong><em>Ordinary Joe</em></strong> and <strong><em>La Brea</em> </strong>for this fall, along with the new <strong><em>Law &#38; Order: For the Defense</em></strong>. In fact, NBC has completely abandoned comedy this fall, opting instead to turn Thursday into an all-<em>Law &#38; Order</em> line-up with <em>For the Defense</em>, <em>Organized Crime</em> and <em>SVU</em> taking over the evening.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-659621 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Paramount-Plus-logo-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Paramount Plus Movies\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Paramount-Plus-logo.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Paramount-Plus-logo-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Finally, even though ViacomCBS isn&#8217;t having their upfronts presentation until later this week, word on the street is that CBS will be sending the <em>Silence of the Lambs</em> sequel series <em><strong>Clarice</strong></em> <a href=\"https://deadline.com/2021/05/evil-move-cbs-paramount-plus-1234758581/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">to Paramount+</a> along with the long-running military drama <strong><em>SEAL Team</em></strong> and the supernatural series <strong><em>Evil</em></strong>. What does this mean for the future of CBS network television? We&#8217;re not entirely sure, but ViacomCBS putting an emphasis on streaming at Paramount+ likely means their more exciting shows won&#8217;t shoot for CBS. We&#8217;ll find out after they have their upfronts presentation.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/tv-upfronts-abc-fox-and-nbc-announce-renewals-cancellations-and-series-orders-clarice-more-heading-to-paramount/\">TV Upfronts: ABC, FOX, and NBC Announce Renewals, Cancellations, and Series Orders, &#8216;Clarice&#8217; &#038; More Heading to Paramount+</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/category/features/the-morning-watch/\">The Morning Watch</a> is a recurring feature that highlights a handful of noteworthy videos from around the web. They could be video essays, fanmade productions, featurettes, short films, hilarious sketches, or just anything that has to do with our favorite movies and TV shows.</em></p>\n<p>In this edition, in honor of the late <strong>Charles Grodin</strong>, watch a classic moment from <em><strong>The Tonight Show</strong> </em>with <strong>Johnny Carson</strong> where <strong><em>The Heartbreak Kid</em></strong> star has some playfully combative banter with the late night host. Plus, find out how <strong>Zack Snyder</strong> answers the web&#8217;s most searched questions about him and the films he&#8217;s directed. And finally, watch <strong>Ewan McGregor</strong>&#8216;s transformation into <strong><em>Halston</em></strong> for the new Netflix series.<span id=\"more-672121\"></span></p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"555\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/AT6HIfhwtKo?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>First up, here&#8217;s a throwback clip from <em>The Tonight Show</em> with Johnny Carson where Charles Grodin appeared as a guest in September of 1990. Grodin is meant to promote his book <em>It Would Be Nice If You Weren&#8217;t Here</em> and the movie <em>Taking Care of Business</em>, but instead, the conversation gets a little heated as Grodin challenges the phony format of talk shows and the illusion of friendly banter. It&#8217;s all merely a great bit as Grodin and Carson clearly have fun sparring with each other, and it shows why Grodin was so brilliant when it came to cranky comedy.</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/QDCowfgaHLA?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Next, with <em>Army of the Dead</em> coming to Netflix this weekend, director Zack Snyder sat down to partake in <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QDCowfgaHLA\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Wired</a>&#8216;s autocomplete interview to answer the web&#8217;s most searched questions about him. Does Zack Snyder have any tattoos? How would he describe his directing style? Is he a nice guy? Get the answer to all these questions and more.</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/rvP0jclypaE?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Finally, <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rvP0jclypaE\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Netflix</a> talks to Ewan McGregor, fashion experts, and more to dig into the new series <em>Halston</em>. In the show, McGregor plays fashion icon Roy Halston, and this featurette explores the legacy and impact of his genius in the industry and how the Star Wars actor transformed into the man himself to tell this story.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\"
